The French tram company, at 11 a.m. on February 30, was robbed of a bag of 4,000 yuan in cash in front of the company. After the case occurred, the French police sent detectives to investigate strictly. It was not until 9 p.m. on the 17th of this month that Jin Jiulin, the superintendent of the special agency of the French police department, led detective Zhang Ziying and the patrol officers of the general team, together with the police detectives of the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, first arrested the bandit Qiu Yanshou (24 years old, Funing native) in the opium den at No. 29 Dafang Lane, Fangbang Bridge. According to Qiu's confession, the gang members Yang Yang, Li Zhongxin, Zhu Hanqiang, Qiang Yunpeng, Pan Yuqing, Liu Shaogen, Zhang Debiao, Zhao Zhongheng, Xu Shaogen, Fan Youheng, and Pan Xiangbang were successively arrested in the pavilion room at No. 30 Anshun Lane, Kangti Road, French Concession, and in rooms 8 and 14 of the Xin Dafang Hotel, No. 381 Edward Road. According to the confessions of Yang and others, Zhou Kui and Zhou Lu, a couple, were subsequently arrested on the floor of No. 34 Derun Lane, Chezhan Road, Nanshi, and two pistols and sixteen bullets were seized. Xia Wenfu and Xu Yuecheng were subsequently arrested at No. 480 Fangxie Road. The five people Qiu, Zhou, Xia, Xu, and Lu, who were arrested in the Chinese Concession, along with the pistols and bullets, were sent to the Public Security Bureau for detention. In total, sixteen men and women of the bandit party were arrested. The details of each case were recorded in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday, the police station first sent the eleven bandits arrested in the French Concession to the First Criminal Court of the Second Special District. Judge Sun Penghang conducted a preliminary trial, first questioning the names, ages, addresses, and occupations of the bandits. Then, Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the police station, stated the case and the process of arresting the defendants, and said that there were many criminals in this case and the case was complicated. He requested a rescheduling of the case for a week in order to conduct a detailed investigation. There were also five men and women bandits and pistols detained at the Public Security Bureau, and he requested that the court send a document to transfer them for joint interrogation before filing a lawsuit. The court approved the report and decided to reschedule the hearing to April 1 to investigate and retry. The defendants were still detained.

The Case of Hu Wang, a Young Woman, Accusing Hu Yunfei of Bigamy is Concluded; Sentencing is Scheduled for the Morning of the 23rd 146

Hu Wang, a young woman from Xuyi, Anhui, is 27 years old this year. She hired a lawyer to submit a complaint to the Criminal Court of the Second Special District, accusing her cousin Hu Yunfei, the owner of the Sino-American Department Store at No. 543-545 Fada Road, of bigamy and abandonment. They married on November 16, 1934, and lived together at No. 30 Sandeli, Wansheng Bridge, Ximen, with Zhang Wanyi and Qiu Zhongshan as matchmakers. Recently, Hu suddenly abandoned her and married another woman, Yang Suxin, and has lived together for three years. Unable to bear the hardship, she requested an investigation. After several hearings, the court ruled that because both parties had spousal relationships, it did not meet the self-litigation procedure, and the judgment was rejected. Hu Wang was unwilling to accept the judgment and filed a complaint with the court, requesting that the French police station investigate and file a public prosecution. The police station summoned both parties for questioning and sent detectives on the 14th of this month to [blank], where the police department's lawyer filed a public prosecution for abandonment under Article 310 of the French Criminal Code. Judge Sun Penghang tried the case, but the defendant Hu Yunfei did not arrive, and the court ordered a rescheduling for another trial. The details of each case have been recorded in previous reports. Yesterday was the date for a continued hearing. The defendant arrived with his defense lawyer. First, the plaintiff Hu Wang stated the process of marrying the defendant and being abandoned, and hired a lawyer to file an incidental private lawsuit, claiming that the plaintiff Hu Wang's left eye was blind, and requested that she be given alimony of 20 yuan per month until she was 60 years old, totaling 8,160 yuan. She also claimed that all the evidence had been submitted in the self-litigation case and requested that the case file No. 109 of the 23rd year be inspected. When questioned, the defendant Hu Yunfei denied that he had married or abandoned the plaintiff. He said that his younger sister had died of illness, and his mother was sad, so her mother sent her to his mother as a daughter. Although there had been talk of betrothing her to him as his wife, he did not agree, so it was not carried out. She had been in his mother's house. Last winter, she suddenly went out to hire a lawyer and falsely accused him of bigamy and abandonment, and demanded a lot of money. Because he did not agree, he fabricated accusations. He asked the court to investigate. The court then summoned witnesses Zhang Wanyi and Qiu Zhongshan to the court. After they took an oath, Zhang and Qiu both testified that they had never been matchmakers for both parties. Finally, after the police department's lawyer, the private prosecution agent, and the defendant's defense lawyer debated one by one, the court ordered the debate to be concluded and scheduled the sentencing for 10 a.m. on the 23rd.

General Manager of Nanyang Tobacco Company, Jian Yujie, Accused by Workers 147

Jian Yujie, the Cantonese general manager of Nanyang Tobacco Company, and Feng Jiaxiang, the director of the tobacco leaf department, were jointly accused by Ding Xinglong, a worker in the tobacco cutting department, and hired two lawyers, Yu Xiangqin and Li Baosen, to file a complaint with the First Special Court, accusing Jian of instigating Feng and others to jointly beat them, causing serious injuries. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Ye Shengchao visited the Fifth Criminal Court for trial. Except for Xu Wenlong, who did not arrive, all the defendants arrived and hired lawyer Qin Liankui to defend them. The plaintiff Ding Xinglong claimed that he lived at No. 262 Nanxingli, Baoding Road, and was a worker in the tobacco cutting department of Nanyang Tobacco Company. This time, the company's employee incentive system, which was established in 1931, concerned the issue of bonus custody. At that time, it was agreed that the company and the workers would each elect a custodian to jointly manage the bonuses. Surprisingly, for two years, it has not been implemented. The workers felt that their rights were involved, so on the 25th of last month, they elected 17 representatives to petition General Manager Jian, requesting that the previous agreement on bonus custody be fulfilled. Unexpectedly, General Manager Jian not only refused, but also fired all 17 representatives. At that time, all the workers were indignant when they heard the news, so on the afternoon of the 2nd of this month, they temporarily and spontaneously went on strike for one hour, and requested the factory to quickly reinstate the 17 fired workers. At that time, Feng Jiaxiang, the director of the tobacco leaf department, came and claimed that he had been ordered by General Manager Jian to prohibit the shutdown of the vehicles, and showed a pistol, ordering foremen Zhu Ahua, Xiaogong Xu Wenlong, etc., to wield iron bars and beat me arbitrarily, with fists and feet, causing me serious injuries. I had already gone to the procuratorate of the court on the 4th of this month to have my injuries examined. When questioned, the defendant Jian Yujie stated that he was not aware of the beating. Feng Jiaxiang also stated that he did not beat him. The plaintiff Ding Xinglong instructed the workers to stop the vehicles on that day. The foreman reported it, and I went out to maintain order and prohibited the vehicles from stopping. At that time, the police detectives also came out and arrested Ding Jiang. Zhu Ahua also denied beating him. After Judge Ye verified the confession, he ordered the case to be rescheduled for trial at 2 p.m. on the 26th.

Zou Xiuying's Appeal Points Out that the Judge Has a Problem; The Higher Court Considers it an Insult to Officials and Will Investigate; Jiang Gongjian Arrives in Court to Testify, Yang Ming Fails to Appear Despite Summons 148

Zou Xiuying, a woman from Wuxi, previously filed a case against lawyer Jiang Gongjian for insulting and falsely accusing her in the First Special District Court. After several hearings by Judge Liu Yugui, the result was that both parties were found not guilty. Both parties refused to accept the verdict and appealed to the Second Higher Branch Court. However, in Zou Xiuying's appeal, she pointed out that the original trial judge had a comradeship with Jiang Gongjian and colluded behind the scenes. After reading it, the prosecutor's office of the First Special District Court believed that Zou Xiuying and Zou's drafter of the complaint, Ta Ming (namely Yang Shaobai), had insulted officials and obstructed public affairs. At that time, only Zou arrived in court. Yang Ming failed to appear despite the summons. First, Mr. Guo asked Jiang Gongjian about what happened, and then questioned Zou Xiuying. Zou stated that she entrusted Yang Ming to draft the appeal. Yang did not have a fixed address and lived in a hotel all day, so he could not be found today. Wang Xiaolai Publishes Remarks: Impressions of Visiting the Philippines and Opinions on Aiding the Market 149

After returning from his tour of the Philippines, Mr. Wang Xiaolai, Speaker of the Municipal Council, has been extremely busy these past few days contacting various parties due to the emergence of the market relief problem. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency specifically visited him yesterday to inquire about Mr. Wang's impressions of his visit to the Philippines and his opinions on market relief. He graciously presented the following:

Impressions of the Trip to the Philippines

The delegation to the Philippines included members from the business sector, the education sector, and various other fields. Therefore, we were able to observe from multiple perspectives and gain diverse insights. The daily itinerary in the Philippines has already been reported in various newspapers, so I won't go into further detail. On the second day in the Philippines, we visited coconut oil factories, cigar factories, and ice cream factories. The equipment in each factory was very complete, with capital exceeding ten million. Wages were at least sixty cents a day, and up to one or two dollars. Working hours were nine hours. The cost of living for workers in the Philippines is only about twenty cents a day, so they can often work hard for a few days and then rest for one or two days, without the hardship of overexertion. There are about eight or nine gold mines in the area. We also visited one of the largest, with a mine extending 10,000 feet horizontally and 100 feet deep per layer, totaling 1,100 feet. After donning the miner's clothes, we descended directly by elevator. This mine can produce forty to fifty million in gold annually. The company's capital is six million pesos (Philippine currency). A 1,000-peso share from twenty years ago can now yield a profit of 500,000 yuan, truly a case of small investment yielding great return. Furthermore, the Philippine Chamber of Commerce invited the Chinese Chamber of Commerce and leaders from various industries to a meeting on March 2nd. The most important points resulting from the discussion were six: (1) Tariffs: Goods shipped from China face higher tariffs, making it difficult to compete with other goods. (2) Transportation: The United States and Japan both have their own commercial vessels for transportation, but Chinese merchants have no overseas shipping industry and are often subject to restrictions. (3) Finance: Previously, one Philippine peso could be exchanged for 1.7 taels of silver in China, equivalent to more than one yuan. Now, it is only worth one yuan and a few cents. The sharp drop in exchange rates significantly affects the value of goods. Therefore, exchange rates are a major problem for Chinese goods exported to the Philippines. (4) Goods: The failure of Chinese goods to adapt to demand is a major reason for the failure of foreign trade, and improvements are urgently needed. (5) Organization: Commercial organizations at home and abroad have failed to connect as much as possible. Even within the business community in one place, there is a lack of unity. Furthermore, the government has not been able to fulfill its responsibility to protect commerce, so command and assembly feel quite scattered. Finally, aviation issues were also discussed. While in the Philippines, I also visited the aviation industry. Various aircraft are striving for innovation, while China cannot even obtain them. Therefore, I immediately used this idea to assist the overseas Chinese in the Philippines to work together in aviation and save the country. The overseas Chinese were deeply moved. The school's cleanliness and newspaper offices were inspected by Mr. Pan Gongzhan and others, and there is a separate report. This meeting achieved considerable results in Sino-Philippine commerce. It was immediately decided to organize the China-Philippine Commercial Advancement Association, with six representatives from the Philippine Chinese Chamber of Commerce and six from the Shanghai business community, totaling twelve people, to engage in preparations, as a future mechanism for promoting trade between China and the Philippines. The Philippine prisons were also visited. Men and women are held separately, the former in prisons and the latter in reformatories. The architecture is also special, with four hundred walls surrounding a dusty wall, with paths on the walls, like the battlements of a Chinese city. Therefore, everything in the prison is visible from the walls. While visiting the prison, I observed military drills and music, rigorous and solemn, which I had never seen before. The training of prisoners is like this, and one can imagine other things. The climate in the Philippines is hotter, especially in March and April. Now it is already the summer vacation. When we were there, the temperature was above eighty degrees. The average annual temperature is about seventy degrees. The Carnival is usually held in February. It is said that the Philippine Autonomous Region will be established in mid-January next year, and an Expo will be held at that time. The Carnival will also be held earlier. Our country should participate and set up a Chinese pavilion. This matter should be suggested to the government. The roads in the Philippines are very wide. Except for the marketplace, which is a bit narrow, the usual width is two or three times that of Shanghai, and cars often run three to five abreast, and their number is also very large. Even the scenic summer resort, Baguio Mountain, which is 5,000 feet high, has very flat roads. It takes three hours to drive around by car, like speeding in a large garden, surrounded by mountains, the beauty of the scenery is breathtaking, and the climate is also good, with flowers and trees blooming in all seasons. From Manila, first take a five-hour train, with air conditioning installed, then change to a two-hour car ride up the mountain. The road is lined with coconut and banana trees, which are pleasing to the eye. In addition, the cold waterfalls in the northern mountains are also interesting. Although the waterfalls are not large, they are in a steep cliff, like sitting at the bottom of a well, making people feel the majesty of nature. Those who compete in the arena now feel infinite shame. Chinese people in the Philippines account for about one-tenth of the total Philippine population. If we talk about those with blood relations, it is more than half. Over the years, the relationship between Chinese and Filipinos has been very harmonious. Other customs are simple and frugal. Women also work hard. Heavy objects are carried on the head, without carrying them on the shoulders or in their hands. They can be called strong. In short, in addition to initiating the organization of the China-Philippine Commercial Advancement Association and promoting aviation to save the country, I deeply feel that our country still needs to make progress in construction. In the Philippines, even uninhabited places have very flat roads, while we have densely populated areas but no roads to pass through. They have roads on the mountains, while we cannot even travel on the plains. Also, in terms of planting trees, the forests in the Philippines are very developed, and the trunks are very large and straight, while many Chinese people have hunched backs. Comparing the two, how can we not be ashamed? After leaving the Philippines, I went to Guangzhou to visit the sugar factory. The scale is grand, using sugarcane from Guangdong as the raw material for sugar production. It is said that after the entire plan is successful, it can supply the whole of China and recover tens of millions of yuan in losses. In addition, the power plant, water plant, fertilizer plant, cement plant, sulfuric acid plant, textile plant, various departments for dividing wool, cotton, and silk, and various dyeing plants were visited with the secretary of the Construction Department. Compared to the one cement factory I visited in Guangdong and Guangxi during the Republic of China in 1926, there has been great progress. Commander-in-Chief Chen Jitang governed Guangdong for six years. As a military strategist, he also has political acumen and economic thinking. It is said that the various factories currently being run are all promoted by the government and have been effective. Then, they are made public to the people. Currently, 15% of Guangdong Province's revenue is used to support industry, demarcate factory areas, and gradually expand. If they can persevere, Guangzhou can also become a major industrial zone. Mining is also underway. When I arrived in Guangzhou, I also visited the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, which is magnificent and can be compared with the Temple of Heaven. At Huanghuagang, I presented a wreath. At the same time, Mr. Liu Yazi, who went from the Philippines to Guangdong, composed more than two hundred poems, which can be used as a reference for this trip. Hong Kong now prohibits prostitution, which will be completely eradicated by the end of June. The market is also very sluggish, and so on.

Opinions on Market Relief

I believe that revitalizing the market is an active action, while relieving the market is a passive approach. To talk about revitalization, the government must encourage domestic goods, and the people must use domestic goods. Otherwise, everything else is not fundamental. As for relief, it should be the responsibility of the government, and silver and money businesses can only assist. After all, silver and money businesses are one of the hundred industries, and their purpose is to operate, not like the government, which should stand in the position of protecting the people. Now, the five million industrial and commercial credit small loan has a chance to succeed, to meet the urgent need. It is hoped that the government will quickly allocate funds to complete this task. As for handling procedures, I think it can be divided into three types. The first type is to support the development of industry and commerce, like a person who is weak and needs nourishment. The second type is to lift industry and commerce out of poverty, like a person who is sick and lying in bed, taking medicine to get up and give him a chance to recover his health. The third type is to seek a good end for industry and commerce, like a person whose illness is hopeless, and to prevent it from spreading. If we can handle things carefully according to this standard, the market will be able to operate. However, industry and commerce should also keep pace with the times. If they stick to old rules, there is no hope of revitalizing the market. Therefore, we should take this opportunity to improve the organization, employ specialized talents, implement scientific management, and then provide relief. Then, there is hope for the recovery of chronic diseases. It's like life. External needles and bait must echo the individual's own training, and then can it be fully effective. If we talk about the present, I hope that government relief, silver and money business assistance, and industrial and commercial businesses receiving assistance can work together to overcome difficulties. Only then can it be effective. For fundamental relief, there must be a sound organization, and then we can talk about the control of various industries. Without control, there is not enough to talk about the entire plan.

Wan Shen Pig Shop Manager Returns to Shanghai Safely After Escaping Recently. Demanded a Ransom of 100,000 Yuan and Was Imprisoned Tightly When Initially Kidnapped. Endured Great Hardship for More Than Half a Year. 150

Wan Shen Fresh Pig Shop in Wusong is the first to open in the Song area, with the oldest brand and prosperous business. It has a Wan Shen branch in Yangjing Town, Pudong, Shanghai. The general manager, Xu Hongjun, is over fifty years old and from Ningbo. Due to business relations, he often went to the Huaibei area to buy live pigs (commonly known as Huai pigs) and transport them to Song for the market. In August last year, Xu went to Huaibei to buy pigs again. He encountered bandits in the countryside near Taoyuan Suqian above Yangzhou and was kidnapped. The bandits then sent a letter to Li Shen Xing, demanding a ransom of 100,000 yuan. However, although Xu has been the manager for many years, he loves alcohol and has large household expenses, so he has no savings. In addition, the bandits demanded too much, so Xu's family had no way to raise such a large amount of money and had to ignore it. However, Xu has been kidnapped for half a year, and the news has been very quiet recently. Unexpectedly, the kidnapped manager Xu suddenly escaped from the bandit's den the other day and returned to Shanghai safely. The shop's employees were overjoyed to see the manager suddenly return. After inquiring, it was learned that he had escaped while the bandits were not paying attention, which was fortunate. According to Mr. Xu, he suffered a lot in the bandit's den, which is hard to describe. At first, the bandits thought I was a wealthy man and demanded 100,000 yuan. The surveillance was tight. Even the sound of a cough was not allowed to be loud, otherwise, beatings would be imminent. The food was very poor and difficult to swallow. The bed board was only two feet wide, and I had to sleep with two bandits, so my body was full of lice. Recently, the bandits found out that I was not rich, and it had been a long time, so the bandits were gradually relaxed, and I was able to take the opportunity to escape, which was a great fortune.

The Lin Xing, a small towing barge of the Songhu Maoxing Company, sailed to the Duck Nest sand sea off the Sanjia Water mouth of Wusong at about 10 p.m. on the 14th of this month, intending to tow a timber ship from Fujian to Shanghai. Grand Event of the Charity Dance Party at the Paramount Hotel 158

Hu Xiyuan and Others Initiate China Electric Light Bulb Reorganization Company 166

Xin Sheng She reports that in China, various businesses often spring up one after another as soon as there is a slight profit to be made, until they destroy each other and perish together. The electric light bulb business was first manufactured by the Yabuer Factory more than ten years ago. Afterwards, imitators sprung up, leading to chaotic market prices and uneven quality. Mr. Hu Xiyuan, a giant in the electrical industry, deeply understands that reorganization is impossible without implementing control. Therefore, he invited more than ten core members of the light bulb industry, including Chen Zinan, Li Qingxiang, Xia Yingde, and Ying Kui, to jointly initiate the organization of the China Electric Light Bulb Reorganization Company, with a temporarily fixed capital of 100,000 yuan. Detailed regulations have been formulated regarding the raw material procurement, manufacturing, and sales of each electric light bulb factory, with a comprehensive reorganization plan. It is heard that after several discussions, if there are no other unexpected obstacles, it will be implemented.

It is also found in soybeans, so there are animal and plant-based types. However, the efficacy of the plant-based type is far inferior to the former, and commercially available animal-based lecithin often contains impurities and is not suitable for injection. It is the most reliable and effective tablet and has long been famous worldwide. Special Announcement

Bank's 1934 Business Report (7) 174

(4) Unemployment and Bankruptcies: If we examine non-gold standard countries, the unemployment and bankruptcy statistics since 1932 show a consistent downward trend except for Canada. This is in contrast to the phenomenon in gold standard countries and is sufficient to illustrate the improvement in social and economic conditions. For example, in the late 1932 and early 1933, the most serious period of unemployment in the United States, the estimated number of unemployed people reached over 13.6 million. The highest unemployment rate reached 35%. Subsequently, with the government's efforts, it gradually decreased. By June 1933, the unemployment rate had dropped to 31%. In 1934, the average unemployment rate was 26%, and the number of unemployed people was less than 10 million.

Li Kangbo Sues Prostitute Zhong Sanyuan for Disrupting Family 175

The First Special Court's Trial Concluded Yesterday, with a Sentence Scheduled for the 23rd of This Month

Li Kangbo, from Shandong, works as a customs broker in the French Concession. His wife has always lived in his hometown. Li, unable to endure the loneliness of being away from home, became acquainted with Li Laosan, a prostitute in a brothel. They rented a place at No. 226 Chongqing Road, Xinzha. Laosan knew that he was wrong, but Kangbo was only 37 years old, and the age difference was more than ten years, so Kangbo was naturally dissatisfied. Therefore, he continued to visit brothels, seeking beauties to relieve his sexual boredom and fully satisfy his desires. He met a prostitute named Zhong Sanyuan in Qunyu Fang Brothel last summer. She was only 29 years old, petite and clever, and Kangbo admired her greatly. After the Mid-Autumn Festival, he spent more than 3,000 yuan to redeem her and hid her in Chongqing Road, living with Laosan. The two had similar backgrounds and should have gotten along, but although Yin and Xing did not avoid each other, the mistress and concubine could not live in peace. Sanyuan suddenly left on December 25 of the lunar calendar and lived with her father, Zhong Degui. She then hired a lawyer to send a letter to Li Kangbo, declaring that she would permanently sever the relationship. Li lost both his money and his love. The next day, he reported to the Chengdu Road police station, saying that Sanyuan had taken gold and diamond jewelry and fur coats worth several hundred yuan and fled. He then hired a lawyer to file a criminal self-accusation against Zhong Sanyuan and Zhong Degui for disrupting the family and stealing clothes and jewelry. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui of the First Special District Local Court opened a trial. Li Kangbo first stated that he suffered from a throat ailment and was afraid to speak. The facts of the accusation were already listed in the complaint, and he asked his lawyer to present the case. He then briefly described the process, saying that he had taken Sanyuan as a concubine on August 16 of the lunar calendar last year, but she suddenly took clothes and jewelry and fled on December 25. Neighbors had seen Sanyuan carrying a package of clothes out the door and handing it to her father, Zhong Degui, to take away. He now demanded that Sanyuan return home and return the clothes and jewelry she had taken, etc. However, according to Zhong Sanyuan's statement, she was deceived by Li to his home last Mid-Autumn Festival. Li said that he had no wife, but in fact, Li had a wife in his hometown, and there was also a mistress, Laosan, in Shanghai, so she refused to be Li's concubine. However, because she was closely monitored by him, she could not escape. Until December 25, she felt unbearable to be abused by Laosan, and Laosan even issued an eviction order. She took the opportunity to return to her mother's home alone and did not take anything. Counting the four months she lived with Li, Li did not give her a single piece of clothing or jewelry. Li was at home and saw her leave. If she had taken something, why didn't he report it to the police that day, and only accused her of theft after she hired a lawyer to formally notify him, etc. Zhong Degui also stated that his daughter was originally in a brothel. It was not until midnight on December 25 that his daughter suddenly returned home and cried about being deceived by Li Kangbo. Only then did he know that his daughter had lived with Li. His daughter was not yet an adult, so he even planned to accuse Li of enticing an underage girl to leave her family. After the lawyers of both parties argued, Judge Liu instructed them to wait for the sentence on the 23rd of this month.

Implementation Procedures for Children's Year 192

Decision to Divide into Three Periods

(Nanjing, 19th) Representatives from the Ministry of Internal Affairs, the Ministry of Education, and the Ministry of Industry met in the Ministry of Education this morning and decided on the implementation procedures for the National Children's Year, dividing it into three periods: the first period from April to the end of July of this year for preparation, the second period from August to the end of July next year for implementation, and the third period from August to the end of October next year for conclusion. The three ministries will present it to the Executive Yuan for approval before announcing the full text of the implementation procedures.

(Nanjing, 19th) The implementation procedures for Children's Year were passed on the 19th. The candidates for the committee are stipulated to be three appointed by each of the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Internal Affairs, two appointed by the Ministry of Industry, and five to seven people hired from children's organizations and those who advocate for children's careers. In addition to the Central Party Headquarters being responsible for guiding the committee, a secretary-general and five to seven secretaries will be established. The funding is set at 50,000 yuan. The Central Committee for the Implementation of Children's Year is limited to being established by June 15th.

Scout Curriculum Not Listed as Required Subject in Elementary Schools 195

Students Participate Freely

Regarding the case of requesting the inclusion of the Boy Scouts as a required subject in elementary schools, the Ministry of Education replied to the China Boy Scouts General Association on November 10 last year, stating that the case was approved, and the Nanjing Special City Council requested that the elementary school senior grades' preliminary scout curriculum be included as a required subject. After review, most elementary school students are from poor families, and it is not easy to bear the various expenses of the Boy Scouts, and there are many subjects, which are difficult to balance in terms of intelligence. Students should still join voluntarily. Recently, the China Boy Scout General Association, based on the resolutions of the council, requested the Ministry of Education to include the young Boy Scouts in the elementary school required curriculum. According to the news from the Ministry of Education, this matter is still based on the actual situation of elementary school students (such as the difficulty of bearing the burden due to poverty and the difficulty of balancing intelligence, etc.), so the Boy Scouts are not listed as a required subject in elementary schools, and students are free to join.

National Central University Relocates Expenses to Be Listed Next Year 198

The National Government recently issued orders to the Executive Yuan, the Control Yuan, and the Accounting Office of the government, stating that the case was approved by the Central Political Conference on March 8, 1935. The case was approved by the government and transferred to the National Central University for the estimate of continuing expenses for the construction outside the suburbs. After being submitted to the Finance Group for review, it was reported that the required continuing expenses for this case were originally submitted by Note Committee Member Zhao Ming and others and resolved in principle at the fourth plenary meeting, and the Executive Yuan was responsible for handling it appropriately. However, the competent authorities did not submit a report on the handling situation. At the 420th political meeting, Committee Member Luo Jialun requested a discussion and resolved that the Executive Yuan should still implement it this year. The competent authorities then submitted a full-year estimate of 960,000 yuan in accordance with the resolution. The government's accounting office reviewed and believed that the submission was late and proposed to change it to six months and 480,000 yuan to be approved from January 1935. After reviewing that the principles of this case were passed by the plenary meeting, and the starting period was also resolved by this meeting to be this year, it seems that there is no problem in approving the listing of these continuing expenses from this year. However, since it was not included in the national general estimate for this year and needs to be paid from the national first reserve fund, there was another 431st political meeting resolution after the 420th meeting on the payment of the second reserve fund, stating that new facilities should be limited to those that cannot be delayed this year. It was not stated whether this case cannot be delayed, and the remaining balance of the second reserve fund is already less than 480,000 yuan, with more than four months left until the end of the year, and it is difficult to guarantee that there are no expenses that cannot be delayed and must be paid. Moreover, once this continuing expense begins, it is inconvenient to stop it midway. It seems that it should be temporarily postponed this year, and the competent (education) department should list it in the 24th-year estimate in accordance with the case. After review, the 447th meeting of this conference resolved to pass it in accordance with the review opinions. Correspondingly, the case was recorded and sent to Yuan Qing to review and transfer the order. It should be handled accordingly except for the reply and the division of the lines. He ordered the college (or Yuan Zhuan) to forward the review to the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Education for compliance.

National Road Construction Association Essay Competition on Highway Issues 204

Sends Letters to University Students Seeking Participation Hires Shen Yi and Others as Judges

In order to improve highway construction and its relationship with rural areas, the China National Road Construction Association is holding an essay competition and sending letters to students from universities across the country to participate. Here is a summary of its regulations: (1) The essay is divided into two topics: one, how to build the most economical and practical highway; and two, can developing highways save rural areas? Participants may choose one topic. (2) The essay should be written entirely in Chinese, with clarity and fluency as qualifications. Each essay should be limited to 10,000 words. Regardless of whether it is selected or not, the original manuscript will not be returned. (3) The essay must be written on graph paper. If there are photos, charts, etc., they should be attached separately. (4) All essays must be sent to the association by June 20th, 1935. (5) The submitted essays will be judged separately by experts hired by the association. The names of the judges are as follows: Shen Yi, Gao Enhong, Ye Gongchuo, Dong Xiujia, Zhao Zukang, Li Zhaohuan, Fan Guang. (6) After the essays are selected, the number of people selected will be limited to ten. The award method is as follows: the first place will receive a bonus of 100 yuan, the second place will receive 50 yuan, the third place will receive 20 yuan, and the fourth to tenth places will receive a full set of books published by the association and a year's subscription to the Road Monthly. The names and photos of all the selected people will be published in the Road Monthly and will be kept by the association as a souvenir.

Page 14

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 208

— (Tian Zai)

"Happiness" must be sought from pain, otherwise, what is obtained is only superficial; because without the vast sea, there is no lofty mountain. In times of extreme joy, one will definitely open one's mouth wide and "haha..." laugh, but when it is really unavoidable, one can also show a smile, but this is a terrible bitter smile!

People all look forward to happiness, but do not know that the object of happiness is suffering. As a result, those who yearn often fall into the net of sorrow.

No Taboos 209

— Master of the Yiyi Studio

In the old-fashioned families of our China, nine out of ten homes have a red paper, ink-printed slip of paper pasted on the walls, even on the door jambs of the front and back doors, with floral patterns around it. This is called "No Taboos."

Naturally, the meaning of "No Taboos" is because our China is a country that advocates "superstition." Every action, every smile, has "superstitious" taboos. Ordinary "clever people" (?) devised this "No Taboos" gadget to avoid trouble, simply to indicate that there are no taboos on anything. If one family does this, and everyone does this, thinking about it carefully, how can we blame the Chinese people for putting on "No Taboos" performances everywhere to satisfy the curiosity of foreigners?

For example, on the walls of every lane on the road, it is clearly written "Urination Prohibited Here." However, right under the words "Prohibited from Urinating," there is a large yellow stain of urine, forcing you to cover your nose and pass by! This is the achievement of our Chinese people performing under "No Taboos."

For example, on boats, cars, or in public places, it is clearly marked "No Spitting." However, even with the words, phlegm and snot are still "spit everywhere!" For example, Mr. A feels an itch in his throat, then coughs, followed by a mouthful of phlegm on the ground! For example, Mr. B's nasal passage is stimulated a bit, causing him to sneeze, and his snot flows out, so he pinches his nose and presses it to the ground, making you look askance, but he doesn't care! This is the ugliness of our Chinese people performing under "No Taboos."

Alas! In short, there are many examples of "No Taboos!" You only need to pay attention and observe anytime, anywhere.

Beside the Grand Canal 210

— Tang Zenggeng

Early morning, the sun of early spring, the wind of early spring. People emerge from the harsh cold of the winter god, straightening their bodies. Fish turn their white bellies in the water. The bustling banks of the Grand Canal are shrouded in the loving tenderness of the spring god.

Here, beside the Grand Canal, is an ordinary event:

A child of eleven or twelve years old selling fried dough sticks, wearing a set of worn-out clothes, carrying a basket in his right hand, he opens his throat and shouts for his life, hoping that in such shouts, he can do more business and earn a few more coins.

The child stands on the bow of the boat, craning his neck to look at the steamer coming in front. When the steamer gets closer, the child desperately jumps onto the trailer behind the steamer. Who knows that the boat is moving, and his footing is unstable. This poor child, along with the basket, the fried dough sticks, and the copper coins in the basket, falls completely into the river. The people on the boat, apart from an "ah ya" sound, do not offer any rescue. Fortunately, the child can swim, struggling for his life in the water. The fried dough sticks float away with the water, and the copper coins sink to the bottom of the river. Although he is struggling in the water, he still tries to grab those fried dough sticks. After some time, a soaking wet child finally climbs ashore, staring foolishly at the few fried dough sticks that floated away and he couldn't catch.

The child is covered in water, and his face is full of sorrow. He stands there silently, his eyes always fixed on the fried dough sticks in the river, already wet and soft in his hands. He falls into endless grief. He has to worry about his master's beating and scolding, and he also worries about where the money for the fried dough sticks will come from. A very lively child now stands there blankly, thinking, without moving or making a sound, two lines of tears hanging from his eyes.

While the child is still standing blankly on the riverbank, small boats are desperately searching for copper coins in the river. They are happy because they have an unexpected harvest. Who cares about the child's pain? Fortunately, there are a few kind gentlemen who give the child some money and send him on his way home.

This ordinary event lingers in my mind. I feel that the world is full of misery, and there are countless suffering children!

Interesting Anecdotes About Wonton 211

— Zui Chi Sheng

My friend, Mr. Jin, is from Taicang and works as a teacher in this city. The other day, I met with him in a restaurant, and he told me a story about a rich man in Taicang: It was quite interesting. So I wrote it down to amuse the readers.

This rich man's surname is Chen, and he has assets of hundreds of thousands. But he is by nature stingy, and he is also very frugal with himself. He never takes a sedan or a car when he goes out. Even for dozens of miles, or more than a hundred miles, he always runs. When he is a little hungry and thirsty from running, he does not go to a restaurant to eat, nor does he go to a teahouse to drink tea. However, if he passes by a small teahouse on the way, he will sit down. People think he will finally order tea, but he doesn't. He takes out two large sesame cakes from his side and asks the waiter for a glass of boiled water. He eats and drinks, eats the cakes, and then continues on his way. His other frugality can also be inferred. One day, he went to the countryside to collect rent. When his family members saw that he was not at home, they made "Shepherd's Purse and Meat Wonton" and prepared to feast. Unexpectedly, as soon as the wonton were made, someone came to report that the old man was back, and they could see him walking from afar. This made the family members anxious and helpless. But the mistress (his old wife) had a good idea, saying: "It doesn't matter, I have a trick to deal with him. And punish him to do hard labor, so we can still eat wonton in peace." She said: "Order the old nanny to take a liter of rice and scatter it on the square in front of the door." The larger the scattered area, the better. The old nanny did as she was told. When the old man arrived at the door, he saw so much rice on the ground, with several sparrows pecking at it. He felt a pang of heartache and muttered: "Alas! Who wasted this rice? It's really outrageous!" Saying this, he bent down and picked up the rice grains one by one, putting them in his pocket. By the time he had picked up every last bit of rice, the wonton inside were cooked and ready to eat. Poor him, patting his back, he was still unaware.

Miscellaneous Talk

Kites of Pinghu 212

— Xingzhi

Once spring arrives, children everywhere are happy. On the green grasslands, they carry kites shaped like centipedes, butterflies, old men, and even new-fashioned airplanes, going out in groups to fly them high. What a delightful thing it is. In my hometown, there is a saying, "Crack melon seeds in the first month, fly kites in the second month," which shows the joy of this season.

Flying kites is an entertainment activity for children, but unexpectedly, farmers in Pinghu also have this elegant hobby!

I heard my colleague, Mr. Cai, say: "The kite that I can't forget the most is the kite of Pinghu."

"Every year in February and March in Pinghu, the peach blossoms are in full bloom, the rapeseed flowers cover the ground like gold, and the green grass is boundless. A group of farmers walk out of the thatched huts, each holding a large paper kite. Although these paper kites are not decorated very beautifully, they are larger in area than ordinary ones and are made much more sturdily than those bought in the market. Usually, the centipede style and butterfly style are the most common. After taking them out, they take advantage of the wind to fly them up. The kite strings are very long, mostly twisted by them in their spare time. The material is mostly hemp, so it is very tough and rough. Ordinary people use only one ball of kite string, but they often use a basket."

"Imagine! A kite string requires a basket, isn't that a considerable amount?"

"When they go out to work, they often fly the kites, letting them soar high in the sky, one by one, carefree and at ease. And the kite strings are tied to the trees. On the bright, colorful plain, a few artificial birds are dotted; before going out to work, they hang up a flag to comfort their minds. Imagine what a meaningful entertainment this is! They only take back the kites they flew at dusk when they go home."

"These kites also have a special kind of interest. Each kite has a bow. This bow is made of thin bamboo, with a hole through the middle section, and then bent, fitted with a thin copper or white rattan string, hung high on the kite tail string, vibrating in the wind, making subtle sounds. Lang lang lang..., ling ling ling..., kong kong..., fast and slow, high and low, coming out with the wind, like celestial music, the elegant sound of the human world, really able to absorb people's souls!"

"Several years ago, I walked through Pinghu and often saw such fun farmers' kites. The kite that I can't forget the most is the kite of Pinghu."

He said such a long passage about Pinghu's kites, which made me unable to help but yearn for it. I never thought that hardworking farmers would have such an elegant hobby! However, in these days of rural destruction, I don't know if the farmers in Pinghu still have the elegant hobby of flying paper kites as before?

Misty Records of Imperial Incense 213

— Originally by Princess Deling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Then, many eunuchs went outside the garden to carry back several loads of fresh mulberry leaves. But even after carrying them back, they could not be used immediately; they had to be carefully washed one by one with lukewarm water that was not too hot, making sure that there was no dirt left on the leaves. Each large bamboo tray of silkworms must be carefully tended by two girls: When one is washing the mulberry leaves, the other uses a clean towel to dry the washed mulberry leaves, laying them flat on the bamboo tray. As soon as the silkworms see the mulberry leaves, maybe they don't see them, but touch them with their feelers, they immediately open their mouths and chew vigorously; if you put your head down a little, you can see their mouths moving non-stop very clearly, and you can see them eating from a very small hole, to the point that they can crawl through it with their own bodies, and the time it takes is very short. Therefore, mulberry leaves must be added twice a day: once in the morning and once in the evening: and later, they must be added three times.

On the afternoon of the first day of feeding large mulberry leaves, when I went to watch again, I only saw that most of the mulberry leaves in each tray had only some leaf veins left, and a few greedy worms were chewing on the veins; I felt that when the worms were eating mulberry leaves, the shape was really ugly, and we could also hear their chewing sounds. And in these large houses dedicated to raising insects, there are probably thousands of silkworms or more, so when we walk in, we can hear bursts of rustling sounds, as if raindrops are hitting dry grass. (272)

Little Western Paradise 214

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Yang Wanhua said: "Sir, you should know the saying that hunger and cold breed thieving thoughts? To be honest, when I first came to Xi'an, I lived in a hotel and spent a lot of money. I didn't expect that in a year, I would fall into such a state." Jia Duocai said, "You have been in Xi'an for a year. Why did you come to Xi'an?" Yang Wanhua had raised her head, but when he asked this, she lowered her head again. Although she had even done petty theft, she still blushed and felt ashamed. After a pause, she continued: "Mr. Jia, do you think I look like a young lady in this state? I've been married for a long time." Jia Duocai said, "Is your husband not in Xi'an?" Yang Wanhua said: "My husband is a businessman. He opened a shop in Nanjing and could have made a living. It was my fault. I wanted to be a mistress for no reason, so I betrayed my husband and followed a man named Yun to Xi'an. According to that man named Yun, as soon as he arrived in Xi'an, he would get an official position. But after being in Xi'an for three months, he almost didn't even see the face of an official. He didn't bring much money either. After arriving in Xi'an, the money was spent in less than a month. Telegrams and express letters were sent one after another, asking friends in Nanjing and Shanghai to remit money to help him. Although a few friends did remit money, the amount was very small. After spending more than a month in Xi'an, there was really no way out, so he told me that he was going to Luoyang to find a friend, and told me to wait in Xi'an, and he would definitely be back in a week. Originally, I knew that he couldn't even scrape together enough money for his own travel expenses, so how could he take me? Rather than the two of us being trapped in Xi'an and starving to death, it would be better to let one person go out and try to find a way. So when he said he wanted to leave, I didn't try to stop him at all and just let him go like that. Who knew that after he left, there was no news at all, and he just left me in Xi'an." (16)

European Situation Affects General Market in the United States 219

A new foreign firm reports that yesterday (the 18th), the markets for American stocks, bonds, grains, and goods were all affected by the situation in Europe. Stocks fell by more than two yuan before stabilizing. American Telephone and Telegraph reached its lowest point in three years. In the bond market, Belgian public bonds plummeted by five yuan, and German public bonds fell sharply by one yuan. The exchange rate of the US dollar against the British pound group soared, while the exchange rate against the gold standard group declined. The Belgian franc rebounded due to reports that France was prepared to protect the exchange rate of the gold standard group to resist attacks by speculators. The Belgian government stated that the position of the Belgian franc's gold standard was not weak. However, Wall Street speculators believed that Belgium had abandoned the free gold standard because it had restricted the export of gold and foreign exchange. The pound sterling's sharp drop of five points caused confusion in the commodity market. Most of the selling came from abroad. Sugar was the only exception, rising due to the unrest in Cuba. Total trading volume for the day was 590,000 shares.

Second Severe Fall in American Cotton 221

—Over 50 Pounds Sterling—

Yesterday, US cotton fell sharply again due to large-scale selling by foreign firms, unfavorable news from Liverpool, and instability in foreign politics and currency systems. This caused many long positions to be painfully liquidated, and factories increased short selling to preserve cotton and textiles. Demand from within the industry was strong, with buying in the middle of the day, but the public lacked confidence in the government's cotton policy, and there was no improvement. Later, some short positions were covered, and the market stabilized slightly, but it eventually weakened again due to public selling. Spot demand was weak, and deliveries were not high. The textile industry was unstable, but there was hope for changes in handling fees. The closing was extremely weak. Spot prices fell by 55 pounds sterling, and futures prices fell by 43 to 58 pounds sterling. British spot cotton fell by 10 points, and futures prices fell by 29 to 31 points. Indian cotton initially fell due to selling by European exporters, but then rebounded due to speculative buying. Page 16

Free Talk

A Chinese of the Oblomov Type 228

— Xihe

There are many among us who waste their years in hesitation, doubt, and laziness, ultimately accomplishing nothing. We want to describe this morbid state, but cannot find suitable words; we want to correct this shortcoming, but cannot find the root cause; there is undoubtedly something missing from this life, but we do not know exactly what is lacking. Perhaps our gaze turns to literary works: Pushkin's Onegin? No. Shakespeare's Hamlet? No. Turgenev's Rudin? Somewhat similar, but not quite. It is merely a kind of inactive weariness, a chronic ailment of those with good talent, good education, and a good environment, yet fail to rouse themselves. Although we do not understand it, this chronic ailment is deeply entrenched in the foundations of our lives.

This question is answered for us by the Russian Goncharov in his famous "Oblomov." This book describes a nobleman of the 1850s, who owns hundreds of serfs, but is by nature lazy and does not manage his estate at all. His servants, close friends, and doctors all try their best to free him from his lazy state, but to no avail. Later, he falls in love with a woman, but is too lazy to go through with the marriage because he fears the trouble involved. As a result, the woman leaves him, and he lives with another girlfriend, eventually dying of a chronic stroke. Throughout his entire life, he never encountered any problems with hunger or cold, and never even put on his own socks. It's not that he had no ideals, but he retreated whenever he encountered harsh reality. When it came to work, all his excitement cooled down. He believed that the world did not need to be reformed, and was satisfied with preserving his estate filled with the air of sleep. "At times, in the depths of his heart, he cried intensely for the sorrows of mankind. He felt an indescribable suffering and sorrow, and yearned to go far away." But in the end, he would not even do something as small as moving, and finally retreated back to his comfortable fortress. When his lover parted from him, she said to him: "...You are as gentle as a dove, you put your head under your wings and ask for nothing more. You are prepared to coo under a roof for the rest of your life." Yes, he was such a person, his whole life filled with an attitude of indifference, a lack of love for struggle and progress, unresisting and yielding to being subjugated, idly wasting his golden years, and falling into the grave without accomplishing anything.

The reason for this is that he was only a "head person," a "mouth person," and not a "hand person."

What a profound lesson this work should be for us! Being too lazy to do anything, only thinking, thinking, and confining oneself with conservatism, is not only a chronic ailment prevalent in Russian life. As an Oblomov who does not rouse himself to self-help, he can find many friends in our ancient China. Those who ignore reality, focus on the void, and leisurely let the years pass, have long exhausted the spring of life and lost their foothold. For these human superfluities, we feel that there is nothing to say but sigh.

Human history increases in beauty and grandeur because of the constant striving for advancement. It is like the mythical Arabian bird Phoenix, spreading its two pairs of wings and rushing into the flames, in order to shed its old self and emerge with a new life. Such a life of striving and effort is the main reason why humans become the "spirit of all things," isn't it? But Oblomov was not fortunate enough to share in the glory and joy of creation. I think there must be many Oblomov-type people among us, or at least, there is some Oblomov blood flowing in our veins. But such a work and character, in terms of teaching and enlightenment, is undoubtedly one of our best mirrors.

People and Books 229

— Hanfeng

On Novels

Almost every book discussing novels mentions three great works: "Dream of the Red Chamber," "Water Margin," and "The Scholars." Although opinions differ, none are as marvelous as those of Cao Muguan, the principal of Shanghai Chengzhong Middle School. Readers of "Yu Si" (Gossip) will likely remember this Mr. Cao. In 1924, he wrote a letter to the editor of a magazine, commenting on these three books with the annotations: "A novel of sexual desire: 'Dream of the Red Chamber'; A novel of thieves: 'Water Margin'; A scientific novel: 'The Scholars'." In recent years, it is feared that he is the only one who analyzes novels in this way. I remember that Shen Congwen also had a wonderful comment on novels, which seemed to be published in "Yu Si," "On Zhang Ziping." His main idea was that Yu Dafu's novels describe sexual frustration, while Zhang Ziping's novels are a release of sex. For reading these two authors' novels, it is best to read Yu first, then Zhang, so that one can experience the wonders of "frustration" followed by "release." This criticism is extremely humorous, but I wonder if Mr. Shen's purpose in writing this article was only to "be humorous."

"Whither Shall We Go?"

In 1925, Mr. Ye Shengtao, lamenting the suffering of the times, wrote a reflection called "Whither Shall We Go Amidst the Many Calamities?" He felt that the era was far from "comfort," and that there was no such thing as "paradise."

"It is so south of the river, and it is so north of the river; it is so east of the mountains, and it is so west of the mountains. Whither shall we go?" He raised this question. He used Yu the Great climbing to the top of a tower to look at the flood as a metaphor. He said, "Although Yu only saw a vast flood in all directions, he never sighed, 'Whither shall we go amidst the many calamities?' He did not sigh, he did not think about the 'whither' question. He felt that this land of many calamities could be transformed into a paradise with few calamities, so he decided on the ambition to control the waters and opened the first page of our nearly four thousand years of history." He was very surprised, "Why do people today only sigh, 'Whither shall we go amidst the many calamities'?" He said: "'Whither shall we go' means 'nowhere to go'." Therefore, in the conclusion, he hoped that every Chinese person would become a "Yu." Mr. Shengtao's meaning is worthy of respect. In a time of "many calamities," there is indeed "nowhere to go." If one cannot become a "Yu," there are in fact only two paths placed before one: "One, to be swept away by the waves and swallowed by big fish; two, to transform into a fish in order to survive in the flood." "Whither shall we go amidst the many calamities?" After Mr. Shengtao raised this question, I feel that it is still necessary to raise it again.

The Seamstress 230

— Linlin

Three hundred and sixty days a year,

Working every day.

No day or night,

No holidays,

Spring doesn't visit this family.

Loneliness supports the small house,

The old clock ticks loneliness.

Second by second—

Stitch by stitch...

Numb feet bent,

No smile,

No words,

Needle cannot break fate,

Ruler cannot measure the years.

Ironing,

Cutting,

A line, a stitch—

A stitch, a line...

Seamstress,

Working every day.

Makes clothes,

Sewn garments,

All worn by others,

Yet she mends her own torn clothes.

What silk,

What satin,

She has no heart to look closely.

Chain of threads,

Thin chest,

Deep thoughts.

Second by second—

Stitch by stitch...

War Miscellany (6) 231

— By Tokunaga Nao, Translated by Ye Yin

Those big Russian devils, all obediently and submissively, grinning, were chased away by the short Japanese soldiers' sharp, quarrelsome-like orders, leisurely and with wide strides heading to the upper rooms, etc.

I once ate the leftovers of those Russian devils. It was millet rice with a lot of vegetable oil.

"Probably Russian devils eat greasy things."

Mother tidied up the basket, her mouth full of chunks of millet rice. As soon as I heard that it was something that the Russian devils ate, I immediately stopped eating it. Moreover, I thought to myself: Can it be that we can't even eat the leftovers of the Russian devils? Although I didn't say it to my mother, I already felt the sorrow and shame of the poor. From that day on, I never went to see the Russian devils again.

(Two)

I felt ashamed that my parents were poor. Unlike a seven- or eight-year-old child, I was very considerate and sensible about things.

Moreover, my relatives were among the poorest in the village. The children of the villagers' peasants would scold me as soon as they saw my face:

"Leftover eater, leftover eater."

I was even beaten up by the youngest son of the landlord, who was much weaker than me, named Shirōji.

Even though I was beaten up, I didn't cry. Even if I cried, I wouldn't dare to cry at home in front of my mother. Because if I cried in front of my mother, I would definitely be beaten again by her.

Once, I cried and went home, so my mother took my hand and brought me to the house of A-Yuan, the king of fights who beat me, and said to A-Yuan's mother, her face flushed with anger:

"No matter how worthless the son of a poor person is, you shouldn't just ignore him when you see him beaten up so bloodily!"

The Crippled 232

— Hu Tianyu

The two brothers had the same illness: half of their limbs were paralyzed, they needed help to walk, and they always shook their heads and twisted their mouths when they spoke, as if they couldn't speak without doing so. Some people called them "a natural pair of treasures."

However, the two brothers also had differences. The elder brother developed the illness after he got married, while the younger brother was born with it. Everyone said: Perhaps the feng shui of their house was bad, which caused both brothers to become disabled.

The woman, in order to cure her husband's illness, decided to dig up the ancestors from the old tomb and bury them in a new tomb. She hoped for a whole year, but finally despaired, because her husband's illness was still the same, neither better nor worse.

This woman was extremely beautiful. She had black eyes and peach-colored cheeks, and a figure that could be described as "healthy and beautiful." But her husband was a cripple, the most useless thing in the world. How could she not be annoyed, sad, and often in tears?

Many people often shook their heads and sighed when they saw her helping her husband walk, saying: "It's really a sin! A fresh flower stuck in cow dung!"

These words pierced her heart, and she couldn't help but feel sad. Poor thing! She had to work even when she was sobbing! The family was poor, what could she do? The two brothers were both disabled and couldn't move. If she didn't find some work to do, wouldn't the three lives in the family starve to death?

A year, two years, passed. The woman's face became thinner with the passage of time.

In the spring of the third year, the elder brother saw that his wife's face gradually became radiant, the clouds of sorrow also dissipated, replaced by a trace of unhidden smile. What was especially strange was that a well-dressed man often came to find her, and she often went out with him.

The elder brother knew that something was not right, but there was nothing he could do. He was a cripple and couldn't control his wife. The younger brother was also a cripple and couldn't help him take revenge.

He passively endured it, pretending not to understand anything. When he saw the man and woman walk out together, he only rolled his eyes and didn't say a word. His only hope was that his wife would not leave him and go.

However, this hope was soon shattered.

That day, when he got up in the morning, he didn't see his wife. He thought she would be back in a moment, but by the afternoon, she was still nowhere to be seen.

The two brothers' stomachs were growling with hunger. They called for people, but there was no response. They couldn't move themselves, and there was no rice in the house. The two of them could only shed tears together.

She didn't come back that day, nor the next day, nor the third day. When would she come back?

A few days later, people passing by outside the house suddenly smelled a foul odor. They walked into the house and took a look. Oh! The two brothers were hanging facing each other, their eyes bulging, their tongues sticking out, their noses and mouths full of purple blood, and their bodies emitting a foul smell...

The bystanders all pinched their noses, frowned, and said:

"Living treasures have become dead treasures! These kinds of people suffer when they are alive, and death is a blessing!"

A Visit to the Oriental Culture Academy (Part 1) 233

— Lanru

A solemn and magnificent building like a palace, shrouded under towering gingko trees, this is the Oriental Culture Academy.

There were seven of us in total who went to visit. After each of us handed over our name card to the receptionist, we were soon led into a Western-style reception room. The most troublesome thing when meeting friends or visiting places in Japan is taking off your boots, but today was an exception. When the messenger gave each of us a pair of overshoes to wear over our leather shoes, everyone's faces showed happy smiles.

These overshoes were made of a piece of yellow canvas, shaped like a small boat, with both ends the same size. The opening of the shoe was sewn with elastic bands, and each pair was the same size. This was difficult for me! If I were allowed to exaggerate a little, both of my feet could fit into one overshoe, but unfortunately my feet were uncooperative, they were not born together.

Although it was only about twenty steps from the entrance to the reception room, the overshoes fell off twice. On one hand, I felt embarrassed, and on the other hand, I felt a little annoyed, as if I had a premonition that today's visit would not be a good one—because this thing was acting strangely.

A thin gentleman in a suit (I forget his name at this time) walked in, greeted us, and then arranged the seven name cards, recognizing us individually like a teacher calling roll. He said many polite words such as welcoming us to visit and asking for guidance.

Next, he reported that the Oriental Culture Academy has two research institutes, one is the one we are visiting, and the other is located in Kyoto with a similar scale. The total annual funding for the two places is 300,000 yuan. The purpose of establishing the Oriental Culture Academy is to study Chinese culture and to promote the popularization and improvement of general culture.

"The process of establishing the Oriental Culture Academy is also very simple," the gentleman said modestly. "Initially, on October 4, 1928, professors from Tokyo and Kyoto Imperial Universities, as well as more than thirty people who were enthusiastic about studying Oriental culture, held a meeting in Tokyo to request the government to establish the Oriental Culture Academy. Soon, they unexpectedly received permission from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the work of the Culture Academy began in April of the following year. Research institutes were established in Tokyo and Kyoto, attached to the libraries and exhibition halls of the two Imperial Universities, and the reproduction of ancient Chinese books began at the same time. Later, the locations of the two research institutes were determined, and construction began. The one in Kyoto was completed in 1930, and the one in Tokyo was completed in the summer of 1933, so we have only been working here for about a year."

He said all this in one breath, and we just listened quietly, sometimes nodding mechanically. He seemed to see that we could not listen to him for a long time due to time constraints, and wanted to visit immediately. So he went out first and brought many copies of the Oriental Culture Academy overview and opening ceremony commemorative postcards to distribute to each of us, so that we could know the general situation inside and avoid being confused when visiting.

This house is really too beautiful! The inside is even more solemn and magnificent than the outside! From the outside, it looks a bit like the Summer Palace in Beijing, China. The stone steps and floors, stone pillars, and walls inside are all built of granite and marble, so when we stepped on the smooth, beautiful, and clean marble, the overshoes were especially easy to slip out of the leather shoes. Two or three people were like me, taking a few steps and squatting down again to pull the two "small boats". Although I felt very troubled in my heart, I could only worry in vain.

Naturally, the main purpose of our visit was to count how many books they have and what kind of books they have, and what they are currently researching.
